  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6685d55f-f02d-46ec-8d81-df67a9a599f6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer7726804221149742608">Lada Dracul has no allies. No throne. All she has is what she’s always had: herself. After failing to secure the Wallachian throne, Lada is out to punish anyone who dares to cross her blood-strewn path.   <span id="freeText7726804221149742608" style="display:none">Lada Dracul has no allies. No throne. All she has is what she’s always had: herself. After failing to secure the Wallachian throne, Lada is out to punish anyone who dares to cross her blood-strewn path. Filled with a white-hot rage, she storms the countryside with her men, accompanied by her childhood friend Bogdan, terrorizing the land. But brute force isn’t getting Lada what she wants. And thinking of Mehmed brings little comfort to her thorny heart. There’s no time to wonder whether he still thinks about her, even loves her. She left him before he could leave her.<br /> <br />What Lada needs is her younger brother Radu’s subtlety and skill. But Mehmed has sent him to Constantinople—and it’s no diplomatic mission. Mehmed wants control of the city, and Radu has earned an unwanted place as a double-crossing spy behind enemy lines. Radu longs for his sister’s fierce confidence—but for the first time in his life, he rejects her unexpected plea for help. Torn between loyalties to faith, to the Ottomans, and to Mehmed, he knows he owes Lada nothing. If she dies, he could never forgive himself—but if he fails in Constantinople, will Mehmed ever forgive him?<br /> <br />As nations fall around them, the Dracul siblings must decide: what will they sacrifice to fulfill their destinies? Empires will topple, thrones will be won . . . and souls will be lost.</span>

<div id="review_1618844157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618844157" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1618844157?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=coverly-love">coverly-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1618844157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5544770819459573356"><blockquote>
  <i>"They are soldiers. They depend upon routine, and anything out of the ordinary will give them pause. And they are men. They hate to be insulted, but they love to hear others mocked. And they are fools, because they cannot imagine that a woman alone in the woods would be a threat."</i>
</blockquote><br/>That was AWESOME. I guess it's my "western" ignorance that keeps me thinking of this series as fantasy. It <i>feels</i>, to me at least, like fantasy. And yet, both <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_' title='And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'>And I Darken</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22817331.Now_I_Rise__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___2_' title='Now I Rise (The Conqueror's Saga, #2) by Kiersten White' rel='nofollow noopener'>Now I Rise</a> are <b>brutal, dark, fictional t</b></span>
  <span id="freeText5544770819459573356" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"They are soldiers. They depend upon routine, and anything out of the ordinary will give them pause. And they are men. They hate to be insulted, but they love to hear others mocked. And they are fools, because they cannot imagine that a woman alone in the woods would be a threat."</i>
</blockquote><br />That was AWESOME. I guess it's my "western" ignorance that keeps me thinking of this series as fantasy. It <i>feels</i>, to me at least, like fantasy. And yet, both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22817331.Now_I_Rise__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___2_" title="Now I Rise (The Conqueror's Saga, #2) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">Now I Rise</a> are <b>brutal, dark, fictional tales based on historical truth</b>.<br /><br />I love this reimagining of Vlad the Impaler as a woman called Lada. I love that Lada is allowed to be every bit as mean and bloodthirsty as Vlad, but also, somehow, <b>demand sympathy from the reader</b>. Well, from me anyway. She stands out as one of my favourite characters from all the YA series I've read in recent years, reminding me somewhat of Adelina from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_" title="The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Young Elites</a>, but she's much nastier than that.<br /><br />This book is - in short - about the fall of Constantinople and Lada's reclamation of Wallachia (you should read the actual history of this, if you're unfamiliar; it is <i>fascinating</i>). It is split into two stories that rarely meet, but both are <b>extremely exciting and compelling</b>. <br /><br />Radu is working as an insider within Constantinople and reporting to Mehmed, but the handsome young Cyprian makes him start to wonder where his true loyalties lie. I love the moral conflicts of Radu's character, and the lessons he learns about life and love along the way. Lada, on the other hand, is <b>so fucking badass</b>. She must fight against all the male nobles and soldiers who dismiss her because of her sex, and she is torn between playing by their rules to gain an advantage, and saying "screw it!" and doing her own damn thing. She doesn't disappoint.<br /><br />I was also pleasantly surprised by the funny banter between Lada and her loyal soldier boys on the road:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>"She is so beautiful," Petru whispered, peering through the hedge they hid behind. "You look nothing like her."<br />Nicolae cringed. "And that, Petru, is why your line will die with you."</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>And THAT ending</b>. Oh my, it was absolute perfection. I don't know what it says about me that I love reading about Lada and her perspective so much. But as much as she is a tough-as-nails murderess, it's hard not to have a certain admiration for her ingenuity and determination.<br /><br />Look, I wouldn't come searching for historical accuracy in this series, but if you are looking for some <b>seriously dark, seriously dramatic thrills</b>-- I cannot recommend these books highly enough.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5544770819459573356" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1792130445" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792130445" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1792130445?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone?? holy shit</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elle by: </span>
      Tori
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2016">z-faves2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-coverporn">z-coverporn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-arcs">x-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-rereads">x-rereads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2016">z-read2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1792130445" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15607649173379847643">this is the gay masterpiece I deserved in the year of our lord 2017 and it is still a masterpiece in 2019<br/><br/><i>And I Darken</i> was a well-written and developed book, but I had mixed feelings on the romance and wanted a bit more in the character department. I did not expect either aspect to improve. <b>I definitely did not expect White to fix BOTH of my issues with book one.</b> It's not often a sequel can surpass my expectations so much, but this sequel is undeniably better than book one. <b><i>Now I Rise</i> both does a</b></span>
  <span id="freeText15607649173379847643" style="display:none">this is the gay masterpiece I deserved in the year of our lord 2017 and it is still a masterpiece in 2019<br /><br /><i>And I Darken</i> was a well-written and developed book, but I had mixed feelings on the romance and wanted a bit more in the character department. I did not expect either aspect to improve. <b>I definitely did not expect White to fix BOTH of my issues with book one.</b> It's not often a sequel can surpass my expectations so much, but this sequel is undeniably better than book one. <b><i>Now I Rise</i> both does away with the love triangle drama and far surpasses book one in terms of character work.</b><br /><br /><b>Lada</b> doesn't get any less fierce during this book; in fact, <b>she gets even more brutal.</b> Yet she's not heartless; she has some very compelling relationship development with several side characters. While she just doesn't have as far to go in terms of development, I still enjoyed her journey and conflict over duty to family. <br /><br />And then there's <b>Radu</b>, who I didn't particularly care for in the first book. Here, though, he got an INCREDIBLE character arc. I am still reeling from this character arc. <b>I cannot get over how much Radu has grown and changed and how much I LOVE HIM.</b> Radu's inner debate over which side truly deserves to win Constantinople really stands out throughout the book, in both his internal and external conflict. It's incredibly difficult to write characters on both sides of the fence, but White executed it brilliantly. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>How many ways could a man turn traitor in a lifetime?</i>
</blockquote><br />Possibly my favorite aspect of the character work were the complex side characters. Between Nicolae, Cyprian, and Nazira, my absolute wife and favorite character of maybe the whole book, I just love everyone. <b>None of these side characters are one-dimensional.</b> Even my least favorite side characters never felt like plot devices; they're all morally ambiguous and they're all interesting. <br /><br />I want to give Nazira an entire extra paragraph. What a fantastically developed character; <b>both an ambitious person who wants vengeance, and a supportive cinnamon roll</b> at the same time. A true lesbian icon. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Hatred makes monsters of us all.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I have to say, <b>Nazira and Radu's platonic relationship development is one of my favorite parts of this book.</b> It is really hard to find such strong and developed platonic friendships in YA. I loved how many characters made comments about how they clearly love each other, but without passion. They're two people who don't always trust others, but they are always so real with each other. And of course, their banter killed me and knocked me into the ground, where I'm still lying full of feelings. I care about their friendship even more than any of the romantic relationships in this book. My favorite kids who mlm and wlw solidarity. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Side by side, and alone together.”</i>
</blockquote><br />There's some great relationship development in this book, too. Lada and Radu and Mehmed's relationships with each other are of course still significant, but the new relationships introduced really stand out. Again, let me mention how much I love Nazira and Radu. But there are so many more! Lada's relationships with her many soldiers and a mentor she finds. But let's be real here: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Radu and Cyprian <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> are the absolute crowning gem of the whole entire book, with so many heartbreaking moments and <b>one of the most incredible slow build relationships I have ever had the pleasure of reading about.</b> But don't worry, <b>this book focuses on romance far less than book one.</b><br /><br />I also LOVE the themes of Radu's section. Everything said about hate and islamophobia is so fucking on point and I love it. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I know it is not rational. None of the people here were responsible for what happened to Fatima. But their mindless hatred of us, their demonizing of Islam, is what let the men do what they did.”</i>
</blockquote><br />And all the themes about religion and its role. This series is so good at discussing religion in a non-offensive way. (Can we talk about how all of these quotes are from Nazira?)<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I think that is Constantinople's problem. They look to a painting to save them. They argue and debate over the state of their souls for the afterlife, while letting the needy in this life go hungry.”</i>
</blockquote><br />The one issue with this book is that Lada's actual plotline is slightly less entertaining in comparison to Radu's. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Since she's already left the capital and become a fierce, brutal warrior, she spends a lot of the book biding her time, and not much forward motion happens at times. Radu's plot never goes two chapters without moving forward. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Part of this may be that <b>Lada's character had her initial character arc last book, while Radu's character had almost all of his character arc in this book.</b> Lada's arc here is slightly more external, where Radu's is both external and internal. It's not much of an issue, though; Lada's chapters would probably be my favorites in any other book. She's still so effortlessly compelling if only through her character development and her badassery. <br /><br />There are a few thematic aspects here that I'm really liking. First of all, I love the emphasis here on working through internalized misogyny. I'd ask anyone who wants even more detail on this aspect to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648618814" rel="nofollow noopener">Simona's review</a>. I couldn't agree more with everything she says. And second of all? <b>The queer rep is <i>so important to me</i></b>. Radu's struggle around feeling like a constant outsider is written with so much care and authenticity, and in this book, the development of Radu and Nazira's friendship just made my life. All the solidarity and all the queer genre fiction that deals with homophobia but isn't entirely about Pain, please. And also, thanks to Kiersten White for guaranteeing that <a href="http://www.gayya.org/2016/06/bury-your-cliches/" rel="nofollow noopener">no lesbians will die in this series</a>. It's a really great guarantee to hear from an author in an environment where my immediate reaction to Nazira and Fatima's existence is "they're going to die, aren't they".<br /><br />And also, can we talk ending? That ending was, emotionally, too much. And I think Kiersten White might have actually added a few details during the arc-to-book transition. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Forehead touching in the farewell scene? AND cheek touching? I WOULD HAVE NOTICED THAT IF IT WERE IN THE ARC. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Basically, this was truly an incredible book, and I can't wait to see where the plot goes next. I love everything about Radu's storyline. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15607649173379847643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2424391772?book_show_action=true">Jun 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-abc-reading-challenge">2018-abc-reading-challenge</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2424391772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2416558639986126745"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567358916i/28084870._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight... You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything.</i>
</blockquote>Lada Dracul - Prince of Wallachia - is <b>ready to rule her country</b>...only that country refuses to be ruled by a Dracul or by a woman. <br/><br/>However, <b>Lada has made her decision, </b>and that is all that matters. <blockquote>
  <i>No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting.</i>
</blockquote> But <b>she cannot rule alone</b> - she has her loyal men, her childhood friend (Bo</span>
  <span id="freeText2416558639986126745" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567358916i/28084870._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight... You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything.</i>
</blockquote>Lada Dracul - Prince of Wallachia - is <b>ready to rule her country</b>...only that country refuses to be ruled by a Dracul or by a woman. <br><br>However, <b>Lada has made her decision, </b>and that is all that matters. <blockquote>
  <i>No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting.</i>
</blockquote> But <b>she cannot rule alone</b> - she has her loyal men, her childhood friend (Bogdan) and...well...that's about it.<br><br>What <b>she desperately needs</b> is the finesse and grace of her brother, Radu. His ease with political intricacies would allow her to take the throne with far less bloodshed...but <b>he is unavailable.</b><br><br>Radu is just as<b> hopelessly in love </b>with Mehmed (the Sultan of the Ottomans) as he ever was. In a desperate bid for Mehmed's love, Radu plunges into the <b>very pits of hell. </b><blockquote>
  <i>[Radu] had imagined Constantinople, had wanted it for Mehmed. It had been simple and straightforward. But now he knew the true cost of things, the murky horrors of the distance between wanting something and getting it.</i>
</blockquote>Meanwhile, Mehmed (happy to get Radu out of his hair) sets off pursuing Lada but little does he know, only Wallachia has her heart. <blockquote>
  <i>The world will destroy her in the end. Too much spark leads to explosions.</i>
</blockquote><b>Wow. I am stunned. <i>Simply</i> stunned. </b><br><br>Kiersten White has done it again - the way she <b>crafts her characters </b>and the way she sets up such intricate plots - I am in awe. <br><br>That being said, the middle of the book did <b>feel a bit stagnant.</b> Lada was all <b>WALLACHIA</b> while Radu was all <b>
  <u>CONSTANTINOPLE</u>
</b> but despite their enthusiasm...they didn't seem like they were going very much of anywhere. <br><br>And yet...that ending though - made up for any and all stagnation! <b>Lada is such a brutal badass. </b> I love it.<br><br><b>A great sequel - through and through.</b> I've <i>got</i> to get my hands on the third as soon as possible!<br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Fiona Hardingham - loved her voice. She did an excellent job with the characterizations!<br><br><i>The 2018 ABC Challenge - N</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2416558639986126745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer5374379721547110673"><b>Let us begin!!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469672010i/19843163.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472408994i/20190710.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>**************THERE WILL BE SOME SPOILERS *************<br/><br/>Okay, so I freaking <b>hate</b> Mehmed! He was alright in the beginning of the first book when him and Lada, and Radu were just friends. And then he becomes Sultan and Lada encourages him and he's a prat! First off, I don't like that crap custom of having the harem. He's in love with Lada but popping out kids. My arse! <br/><br/>And Lada and Radu just keep loving him no matter what. The hell? <br/><br/>Anyhoo, Lada is off trying to get her throne of Wall</span>
  <span id="freeText5374379721547110673" style="display:none"><b>Let us begin!!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1469672010i/19843163.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472408994i/20190710.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>**************THERE WILL BE SOME SPOILERS *************<br><br>Okay, so I freaking <b>hate</b> Mehmed! He was alright in the beginning of the first book when him and Lada, and Radu were just friends. And then he becomes Sultan and Lada encourages him and he's a prat! First off, I don't like that crap custom of having the harem. He's in love with Lada but popping out kids. My arse! <br><br>And Lada and Radu just keep loving him no matter what. The hell? <br><br>Anyhoo, Lada is off trying to get her throne of Wallachia and she's having a very hard time. No one cares for her and no one wants her to be prince. &lt; -- Yes, prince. Assassins are trying to kill her but Lada and her men take care of most of that and then Lada just starts taking her revenge. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Lada knew punishing Transylvania for everything that had gone wrong in the past year did not make perfect strategic sense. But it felt better than anything else, and so Transylvania burned.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I love Lada's men. They are very loyal to her for the most part. Bogdan and Nicolae hold a special place in my heart. I also fell in love with Hunyadi who was an enemy at one time but became a great friend to Lada. Then that b••tard Mehmed happened! <br><br>Lada asked Radu to come to her and help her but he's stuck so far up Mehmed's rear end that he doesn't go. He's in love with the jerk. Once again, what the hell? Mehmed is doing nothing in this book but using Lada and Radu. I really hope Mehmed either takes a turn for the better in the next book or that Lada kills him deader than dead! <br><br>I love Radu's wife, Nazira. She was so much fun and so smart! She had me laughing a few times. <br><br>Then Mehmed sends Radu off to Constantinople, he just sends him out to possibly get killed. I loathe him! Nazira goes with Radu, so there was a whole sh•t show over there. <br><br>Lada goes through all kinds of hell. She even saw her mom which was beyond crazy train! <br><br>There are those that are killed of course and I wish they weren't but it is what it is. <br><br>Then Lada gets her throne and she's not all that happy with the way things have been going. I love her so much. She's bloody, brutal, but she takes up for those that need to be taken up for. <br><br>You better rock it in the next book Lada and not let anyone kill you!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>She had done what was necessary. She watched as each body was removed. She would mark their passing, and acknowledge their unwilling sacrifice. Because with each body they drew closer to her goal. She clutched her locket so tightly that her fingers ached. <br><br>She was a dragon. She was a prince. She was the only hope Wallachia had of ever prospering. <br><br>And she would do whatever it took to get there.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Some court people thought they could tell her what she needed to do. Wellllllll, that didn't work out too good for them in the above excerpt =) <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>To Radu, my brother, <br><br>I do not acknowledge your new title, nor Mehmed's. Tell the lying coward I send no congratulations. He sent none to me when I took my throne in spite of him. <br><br>You did not choose right. <br><br>Tell Mehmed Wallachia is mine. <br><br>With all defiance, <br>Lada Dracul, Prince of Wallachia</blockquote>
</b> <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498681503ra/23151559.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Take that b•tches!<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/06/now-i-rise-by-kiersten-white.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>

<div id="review_2031700221" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2031700221" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2031700221?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2031700221" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9520325569346389519"><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>Nicolae put an arm around Lada, drawing her close. ''Make a deal with the devil until you are both over the bridge.''<br/>''Am I the devil, or are they?''</b>
  </blockquote>
</i><br/>Too often I read YA fantasy series that make me ask myself, ‘‘Why am I reading this book? What is the purpose of this story? Haven’t I read something similar recently?’’ But with this particular series, the purpose is clear. <br/><br/>Lada wants to be Prince of Wallachia. She will stop at nothing to achieve her goal. She will destroy anything and </span>
  <span id="freeText9520325569346389519" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>
    <b>Nicolae put an arm around Lada, drawing her close. ''Make a deal with the devil until you are both over the bridge.''<br />''Am I the devil, or are they?''</b>
  </blockquote>
</i><br />Too often I read YA fantasy series that make me ask myself, ‘‘Why am I reading this book? What is the purpose of this story? Haven’t I read something similar recently?’’ But with this particular series, the purpose is clear. <br /><br />Lada wants to be Prince of Wallachia. She will stop at nothing to achieve her goal. She will destroy anything and anyone that gets in her way. There’s nothing I love more than a determined character. It makes me feel invested in the story. Lada is someone to be both admired and feared. <br /><br />Even when I thought about halting my reading, I couldn’t do that for long. I needed to know if Lada would succeed. Although this is a historical series—not fantasy!—as it’s based on true events, I am unfamiliar with Romanian history. (A shame, really, since I was born there.) So thinking about the fact that what I’m reading is also instructive and realistic sparked my interest. Burst it, really. <br /><br />Radu and Lada are separated for the entire novel. Lada is gathering allies and Radu becomes Mehmed’s spy. The ugly Mehmed. He’s back. He isn’t ugly exactly—but he’s awful. If you hated him in the first book, you will want to strangle him now. <br /><br />The separation is truly felt. Both characters are affected by it and so is the reader. Radu and Lada together are quite something. But at the same time, they are getting older and their futures are getting blurrier. They need to make sure they know where they’re going and how to get there.<br /><br />New characters are introduced. Some allies, some enemies, some somewhere in between. I adored that. Not knowing if someone can be fully trusted spices my reading experience. I liked wondering about people’s intentions and worrying for the protagonists and holding my breath when danger came. <br /><br />Just like the first book, it took me a few chapters to get into the story. I forgot how the first book ended, so I was confused at first. But the beauty is that even if the story is not written from the first person point of view, it still feels as though we’re reading Lada and Radu’s inner thoughts, making it easier to know what they’re thinking and how they perceive everything that is happening. <br /><br />It's so unfortunate this isn’t a TV series. It would be such a winner in my opinion. Plus I would just love to see a kick-ass Lada on screen. Something between a Lara Croft and a Cersei Lannister. Cannot wait for the last book. So sad… last book. Why must it end?<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9520325569346389519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1648618814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648618814" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648618814?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648618814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer350531437759083665"><b>“<i>The daughter of Wallachia wants her knife back.</i>”</b><br/><br/>•Last year, I adored <i>And I Darken</i>. I think its publication was a true event;<b> I don’t know of any other YA historical/fantasy series or standalones that can be said to get close to what <i>And I Darken</i> presented its readers with</b>. Kiersten White had clearly meant her story to stand out as <b>unique</b>, and she succeeded gloriously. Just the fact that her heroine didn’t put love above anything else was impossibly refreshing; the two male protagonists were so </span>
  <span id="freeText350531437759083665" style="display:none"><b>“<i>The daughter of Wallachia wants her knife back.</i>”</b><br /><br />•Last year, I adored <i>And I Darken</i>. I think its publication was a true event;<b> I don’t know of any other YA historical/fantasy series or standalones that can be said to get close to what <i>And I Darken</i> presented its readers with</b>. Kiersten White had clearly meant her story to stand out as <b>unique</b>, and she succeeded gloriously. Just the fact that her heroine didn’t put love above anything else was impossibly refreshing; the two male protagonists were so faceted and fleshed-out, I sometimes wondered at their not bursting out of the two-dimensional page; and the moral greyness of all three of them, paired up with the harshness and the violence of the world they moved in, made me think often of <b>the YA label as a fence this novel sat on rather than respected</b>. <br />In few words,<b> I loved it all</b>. And I would have been satisfied with Kiersten White just confirming all the work she had done in that book, even without any real improvement. Meaning: I am a fool. Because <b>she improved it</b>. <br />Oh, what am I saying? She took all the good things she had put in book one, worked some magic, and the level of the whole series skyrocketed. If the third installment is anything akin to these two books, the Conqueror’s Saga is bound to become a favorite of mine.<br />But I’ve blabbered enough; you’re here for a review, and a review I’ll deliver.<br /><br />•The book follows<b> two plotlines, Lada’s and Radu’s</b>, each of them either struggling with their demons, fighting for their dreams, and sometimes both at once. <b>Lada’s narrative is less rich and paradoxically more static</b> (since she is the one mostly on the road) than Radu’s, and for me it was also slightly less engaging,<b> but her characterization never stumbles, ad it develops</b> in a direction that is as frightening as, to YA readers used to ponies and rainbows, it is unexpected.<br />No one is going to be surprised if I say that <b>Lada is ferocious, cruel, determined to the point of viciousness, to the point of stubbornness</b>. What is probably going to make you wrinkle your nose is that I see in her as much steadfastness and commitment as fear. <b>In my eyes, Lada is fundamentally a very scared young person who has understood the only way she can work her way into the world is not to weave it, but to punch and kick and stab it herself, for herself</b>.<blockquote>“Perhaps she had never stopped being that girl <b>lost in a place where she could never have power</b>.”</blockquote><br />White, indeed, in this book added to her characterization a great many nuances strongly linked to<b> Lada’s sexuality and identity as a woman</b>. The truth is that if Lada could, she would be neither, man nor woman: she is honest when she says that <b>“[She has] no wish to be a man,”</b> no matter how <b>uncomfortable</b> her body and sexuality in general can make her, but, on the other hand<b>, “Better to be a soldier than a woman”</b>. Her relationship with Mehmed is masterfully <b>contextualized in this subtext</b>, and I love White for giving their romance a narrative purpose, instead of doing the opposite, as it happens more and more often, and bending every other thing to it. <b>The dagger</b>, too, which she constantly mentions also metaphorically, is <b>a powerful symbol of Lada’s claim to overcome the limits of gender</b>, not to mention more obvious hints like her title –Prince– or her refusal to be dressed up like a doll. <br />Moreover, her being so viscerally attached to her homeland almost brought tears to my eyes. Sometimes this feeling is concretized in physical elements of the landscape, and those passages stole my breath.<blockquote>“What if she remembered the fortress wrong? What if she climbed up and the sun did not come out? What if it did, but it felt the same as any other sunrise?<br />[...] She would climb that peak one day, soon. <b>When it was all hers. She would come back, and she would rebuild the fortress to honor Wallachia.</b>”</blockquote><br />•My second point about Lada’s plotline concerns <b>a technical aspect</b>. I think <b>it’s meaningful that, when the PoV is hers, the only properly characterized people are women, and men meant to stand for or represent something else</b>. <b>Oana and Daciana</b>, for instance, are hardly recurring presences, but their personalities are perfectly outlined in very few but very skilled strokes. (Daciana, besides, is a stunning female character, and she deserves a whole paragraph only to her praise, but this review is already way too long as it is, so I'll pass.) The same can be said for <b>John Hunyadi</b> (I love you, Hunyadi! I love you!), whom Lada puts in direct contrast and comparison with her late father, to the point that she outright tells him –<b>“I wish you had been my father.”</b> As for <b>her Janissaries</b>, <b>Nicolae</b> is more or less the only one who stands out, if we consider that, after all, <b>Stefan</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[is functional to Daciana characterization <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and <b>Petru</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[was functional to his own killing <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>; thus, Nicolae stands for the Janissaries. And <b>Bogdan</b>, well, he hardly speaks in the whole book: it’s complimentary to say that he is a puppet. When I noticed his flatness in <i>And I Darken</i>, I considered it a flaw, and a very annoying one at that, but I’ve come to think that if White wanted him fleshed-out, she would have fleshed him out with little effort. I think, now, that his character is so bland because Lada does not see him, just as she doesn’t see who doesn’t interest her: <b>she is too self-centered</b>, too power-driven, too angry with the male half of humanity (her problems would basically be gone if she were a man, but she still would rather choose androgyny) <b>to pay attention to who doesn’t directly serve her ambition</b> (I think Nazira’s observations on her and Mehmed were eerily on-point about this). What she treasures, in her own lucid way, in Bogdan, is his loyalty: the only thing she notices in him is his loyalty. You see how, <b>logically, her PoV is faultless</b>. <br />It’s astonishing how <b>an apparent technical flaw</b> can turn out to be an important piece of a wider picture if we only think about it. <blockquote>“They were her people. This was her country. This was her throne. She needed no intrigues, no elaborate plans. <b>Wallachia was her mother.</b> After everything she had been through, all she had done in pursuit of the throne,<b> she was left with one thing only: herself.<br />She was enough.”</b></blockquote><br />•And now, <b>Radu</b>. As I said, his side of the story is more engaging than Lada’s, and surely way more<b> painful </b>too. If I were a tiny bit more dramatic than I am, I’d say it’s <b>excruciating</b>. Let’s settle for <b>devastatingly heart-rending</b> then.<br />I don’t think I know another YA author who is so skilled at staging<b> the “grey zones”</b> of the world: in White’s mind, nothing is all white or all black, and Radu’s perspective show it perfectly. <blockquote>“He knew Mehmed would build something truly amazing. He knew that Constantinople needed to fall for Mehmed to hold on to his empire. He knew that Mehmed was the greatest sultan his people had ever known. But, like his love for Mehmed, it was no longer simple.<br /><b>Radu had seen what it took to be great, and he never again wanted to be part of something bigger than himself.</b>”</blockquote><br />The irony of Radu’s destiny is that, but for the two only people he would sacrifice everything and anything for, the other significant people in his life are all pretty nice fellows. So who do you think he’ll need to betray and put in danger?<br /><br /><b>Nazira</b> and <b>Cyprian</b> are exactly like Radu, i. e., too precious for this world. <b>In the relationship between Radu and Nazira is condensed, I think, all the true, untarnished hope White allowed herself to put in this novel</b>, and it’s lovely and reassuring, how their love for each other can warm the bleakest moments of the story. On the other hand, it was a masterstroke on the author part to give Nazira that touch of, if not cruelty, then need for revenge towards the Byzantines—she would have come off as too pristine otherwise. <br />If Nazira was my present hope, sweet, charming Cyprian is all my future one —<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a single joy, Kiersten. Give us this one single joy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />•A part from Radu’s sorry fate, what is truly unbearable in witness him witnessing Mehmed’s war crimes and the horrors of war, or, as he himself puts is, the <b>“sickness of the soul that turned men into monsters.”</b> Radu’s process of disillusionment is, as I see it, <b>the core of the entire novel</b>: it’s what monopolizes the reader’s attention and what best focuses his sympathy and emotional involvement. <i>And I Darken</i> was Lada’s book, but <i>Now I Rise</i> is unarguably Radu’s, and he takes over the role of true protagonist with no difficulty whatsoever. His moments of doubt, or the ones when he realizes both sides are engaging in unspeakable cruelties and that taking one over the other is not nearly as easy as it was before, are written so as to make them as <b>intimate and raw</b> as possible, <b>as if we were spying into Radu’s conscience</b> through tiny, clandestine holes the author had opened for us, which only adds to our torment, but also to our commitment. <blockquote>
  <b>“Whichever side won, neither would triumph.”</b>
</blockquote><br />•Lastly, in case it still wasn’t clear, I only want to say that <b>I worship Kiersten White</b> and I applaud her not only for her creative work, but also for all the<b> historical research </b> a book like this requires –speaking of which, the only reason this series is labeled as <b>“fantasy” </b>is that it’s a <b>reimagining of actual historical facts</b>, but there’s no magic or anything like that in it.<br /><br />➽ <i>Now I Rise</i> is, in brief, <b>dark</b>, <b>ugly</b>, <b>harsh</b>, <b>brutal</b>, <b>inflexible</b>, <b>disturbing</b>, <b>unsettling</b>, <b>painful</b>, <b>nuanced</b>, <b>difficult</b>, <b>somewhat repulsive</b> and <b>absolutely unputdownable</b> at once. I don’t know how I am supposed to wait so long until the conclusion and I know I’ll be unhealthily obsessed but this story and, above all, these character until next summer (and possibly after that too, but at least the wait will be over). <br />If you still haven’t, for your own good, readers, go catch up with this series now. You’ll see you’ll thank me.<br /><br />*All the quotes are taken from an ARC and are subject to change*</span>
  <a data-text-id="350531437759083665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2605441734?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553522389" href="/book/show/36794660-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2605441734" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17179222924418618824">if you had told me 10 years ago, when i was bored out of my mind in world history class, that i will <i>voluntarily</i> read a series about the ottoman empire and the siege of constantinople (not to mention i would also enjoy myself throughout), i would have said youre crazy. and yet, here i am. lol.<br/><br/>the pacing/layout of this series is so organised and straightforward - i love it! the first book is an intro to the characters and the ascension of mehmed, this one focuses on the siege of various kingdoms,</span>
  <span id="freeText17179222924418618824" style="display:none">if you had told me 10 years ago, when i was bored out of my mind in world history class, that i will <i>voluntarily</i> read a series about the ottoman empire and the siege of constantinople (not to mention i would also enjoy myself throughout), i would have said youre crazy. and yet, here i am. lol.<br /><br />the pacing/layout of this series is so organised and straightforward - i love it! the first book is an intro to the characters and the ascension of mehmed, this one focuses on the siege of various kingdoms, and now im looking forward to seeing how each character will handle their new conquests in the next book. and whilst im finding the historical components more interesting than anticipated, the characters are still why i continue to read these books. <br /><br />i wasnt as connected with lada and her story in this as much as i was with radu, but man. she is one heck of a character. shes so unapologetically savage. nothing will stop her from getting what she wants and i love how she makes a name for herself in a world made for men. but regardless of her intensity, radu is the one who stole my attention and heart. his characterisation and development is so heartbreaking to read. i feel so much for him and his desire to always be there for the one he loves, regardless of the unrequited feelings. but his conflicting struggle to remain loyal to his sister at the same time is so sad. my poor, sweet boy. :(<br /><br />i have become so invested in these characters, more than i would have ever imagined, and i cant wait to read the final book to see how the story will end for everyone!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1920183396" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1920183396" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1920183396?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32717627-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=hate-that-i-love-them">hate-that-i-love-them</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920183396" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9584300779695367506">When I finished the first book in 'The Conqueror's Saga', I couldn't wait to get my hands on the next book. I absolutely loved Mehmed, Lada and Radu. I was completely taken in by their unique personalities and the love that they had for one another. Despite the fact that their interests were often conflicting, they managed to remain the closest of friends, and sometimes more.<br/><br/>However, I am sad to say that I didn't get the same pleasure from reading 'Now I Rise'. It was like this book came along a</span>
  <span id="freeText9584300779695367506" style="display:none">When I finished the first book in 'The Conqueror's Saga', I couldn't wait to get my hands on the next book. I absolutely loved Mehmed, Lada and Radu. I was completely taken in by their unique personalities and the love that they had for one another. Despite the fact that their interests were often conflicting, they managed to remain the closest of friends, and sometimes more.<br /><br />However, I am sad to say that I didn't get the same pleasure from reading 'Now I Rise'. It was like this book came along and burst my bubble. Any seeds of resentment and anger that were planted in 'And I Darken' came to life in this book. My view of these characters has been irreparably changed...and not for the better.<br /><br />One of the things that really stood out to me about the first book was the loyalty that this trio seemed to have for one another. Even as their political and religious alliances were in opposition, they always found a way to support one another and place their personal relationships first. Yes, for Mehmed and Lada there were a few betrayals, but I never felt like they were more than superficial, based upon the expectations of their positions. Perhaps I just wanted to believe that, especially where Mehmed was concerned, even though the writing was on the wall.<br /><br />In contrast to the first book, 'Now I Rise' is full of betrayal and underhanded manipulations. Every one of them turns their back on the people that care for them, some to a greater degree than others. However, none of them were innocent of treachery in this book.<br /><br />Mehmed, in particular, was a character that I grew to despise. He claims to love Lada, but sells her out at every turn. Honestly, I began to dislike him in the last book as he repeatedly chose to sleep with other women while professing his love for Lada. What a pig! I wanted to make excuses for his behavior then, but I've got my head on straight now. This book helped me come to the realization that he is nothing more than a calculating, self-centered, power-hungry asshat! I hope that Lada kills him.<br /><br />Although I like Lada more than Mehmed, she is equally obsessed with power and consumed by her blind ambition to reign. I think I probably cut her a little more slack because she is a big time underdog. It is rare to encounter such a strong, badass female lead character, so I really want to like her. Unfortunately, I found her pretty unappealing for much of this book also. She may not have betrayed Mehmed and Radu in the huge way that they both betrayed her, but she did plenty of horrible things in order to assert her power over those she hoped to rule. The brutal tactics she employed didn't sit well with me either, regardless of the fact that I wanted her to achieve her end goal. <br /><br />Sweet Radu also proved to be a big disappointment this time around. Turning his back on his sister, he willingly submits to Mehmed's every self-serving demand. It was pathetic. He befriends and then betrays close friends in order to further Mehmed's quest to conquer Constantinople. Even as he knows that what he is doing is wrong, he repeatedly chooses to sacrifice others that are innocent in the hopes that he will gain the affection of a man that he knows will never love him the way that he does. I wanted to pity him, but my anger toward his actions never let that emotion set in. In some ways he was every bit as bad as Mehmed, but his duplicity was hidden beneath a façade of presumed harmlessness.<br /><br />After finishing this book, I feel hollowed out. There is a part of me that still wants to see how things will work out. I'd hate to miss it if Lada ends up killing Mehmed. However, a part of me is just disgusted with all of these characters that I once loved. <br /><br />I'm not sure that I can bear to watch them destroy one another. It is clear that this isn't going to be a HEA type of story. The damage is done and I suspect that their insatiable hunger for power and unobtainable love will just end up destroying them all. It is fitting, but not necessarily something that I feel like watching play out. I guess I'll see how I'm feeling when the third book is released. For now, I'm going to lick my emotional wounds and give my disappointment plenty of time to sink in.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9584300779695367506" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1702228239?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1702228239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12419778846790764413"><b>This was so bloody and so brilliant.</b> Like Lada has never had any chill, but she has LESS THAN NONE NOW because wow. This is fantastically dark and twisty and intriguing and also kind of depressing?? I admit I'm not giving it the full stars mostly because I felt...a bit slumped after the end. I shall explain. But just so you know:<b> HOLY WOW I LOVE THIS SERIES A LOT.</b><br/><br/><b>+ The characters are totally what's absolutely caught my heart.</b><br/>Like put in all the HEART EYES here for our Slytherin little children. </span>
  <span id="freeText12419778846790764413" style="display:none"><b>This was so bloody and so brilliant.</b> Like Lada has never had any chill, but she has LESS THAN NONE NOW because wow. This is fantastically dark and twisty and intriguing and also kind of depressing?? I admit I'm not giving it the full stars mostly because I felt...a bit slumped after the end. I shall explain. But just so you know:<b> HOLY WOW I LOVE THIS SERIES A LOT.</b><br /><br /><b>+ The characters are totally what's absolutely caught my heart.</b><br />Like put in all the HEART EYES here for our Slytherin little children. I love how they're devious, but in different ways. <b>Lada</b> continues to be terrifying. At one stage a guy mentions his son needs a wife and her reaction is just: "wtf do I look like I care." Please never never change Lada. She is so unapologetically HERSELF. Violent and driven and fantastic. She gives little girls knives and tells them to be amazing. LADA. &lt;3 &lt;3 Also pls never leave me alone in the same room as her. I would die.<br /><br /><b>+ And Radu? OK, Radu is the reason of the world.</b><br />He is my pure cinnamon son and HIS STORYLINE BROKE MY HEART. I mean, he always breaks my heart but this was just....oh wow. See that puddle on the floor? That's me. <b>I absolutely am B R O K E with the need for him to have some happiness.</b> He doesn't think he deserves to be loved and just...Radu no. <b>His relationship with his "wife" Nazira basically outshines everything.</b> She is perfect, ok. These are the GAY CINNAMON SWEET CHILDREN of the series and I love them. I love how they have such an epic non-romantic friendship and Nazira is kind of crafty. #Nice<br /><br />But...fine...I admit...<b>I honestly think Radu should've gotten a scrap of happiness in this book.</b> I ship him and Cyprius so bad and like...DUDE. IS IT SO HARD TO GIVE THEM A MOMENT. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I needed them to have had more than like that super smol moment they had. They should've kissed ok. Just once. I'm mad because I think balance is needed. Radu is obviously got a tragic story to play out and a LOT of character development still to happen. I'm FREAKING PLEASED he's recognised that Mehmed is playing with him and will never treat him well, so like??? Yas Radu please slap Mehmed and leave. But I WANTED RADU TO HAVE A BRIEF MOMENT OF HAPPINESS GODDDDD. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>+ I hate Mehmed.</b><br />Like. Burning. He's a self-entitled bastard and totally <i>uses</i> Radu's feelings for him to manipulate him into doing anything Mehmed wants. Basically he's queer-baiting and I JUST WANT HIM TO WALK OFF A SMALL CLIFF. NOT TOO MUCH TO ASK. HE'S SO SELFISH AND GREEDY.<br /><br /><b>+ It was like so BRUTAL.</b><br />Book one was intense, but this was more intense. It's not very graphic though (imo) but Lada is getting a throne in the most bloody way possible and Radu is in the middle of a bloody siege. So.<br /><br /><b>+ I also love how Radu and Lada thought of each other.</b><br />I'm peeved they never met up in this book. But they legit spent all this time going "I WISH I HAD MY SIBLING...BUT THEY DON'T NEED ME." Like both of them. Are saying that. For goodness sakes you adorable morons...pls be better siblings to each other.<br /><br /><b>+ Also shout-out to Lada's men. Who are fab.</b><br />Except Bogdan...don't know what he's on about there, but he needs to chill out. Nikolai is BEST. I love how they sneak humour into an otherwise pretty dark tale.<br /><br /><b>+ The siege of Constantinople was so sad.</b><br />I cry into my soup. Except I don't have soup. But if I did = there'd be tears. I really really felt the devastation so...this book. This writing. THIS YES.<br /><br /><b>+ I also loved all the historical detail sin the writing!</b><br />Like the development of canons and stuff?!? It was so interesting. I know this isn't an accurate retelling of history, but I do think I've learned a LOT through this and like the world building and details were so amazing and WOW.<br /><br /><b>+ The audiobook is really good too!</b><br />I actually felt the book went by super fast and the narrator (woman) is really dynamic but not overdramatic or anything. And then it finished and I was a bit put out. How dare u tho.<br /><br /><b>OVERALL: this was a book of STABBY STAB and character development and the darkening of the horizon.</b> I am literally D E A D with nerves about the sequel. I want Lada and Radu to work as a sibling power team and I want Mehmed <s>dead</s> to lose the respect of lada/Radu because he doesn't deserve it. I WANT RADU TO FIND LOVE AND SOMEONE WHO DESERVES HIM <s>(aka Cyprius and him pls)</s> and I seriously want to know how everything plays out with Lada's journey to Princedom and Radu's journey to STOP MAKING ME CRY. I LOVE YOU CHILD. PLEASE FIND HAPPINESS. <b>It's honestly FANTASTIC.</b><br /><br />(Note: Since, as I mentioned, I listened to the audio I have no freaking clue how to spell anything haha. Bless Radu and Lada for their easy 4-letter names. I can do zat.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12419778846790764413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1969388996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969388996" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1969388996?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969388996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1069842736033527943"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896510860' rel='nofollow noopener'>And I Darken</a> ★★★★★<br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969388996' rel='nofollow noopener'>Now I Rise</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143076758' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bright We Burn</a> ★★★☆☆</blockquote><br/><blockquote>
  <i>They had nothing better, nowhere else to go. They were loyal to her, and to the hope that perhaps she would find them a place in the world.</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>FIVE. FREAKING. STARS.</b> <i>Now I Rise</i> is non-stop action, death, war, betrayal, and general bad-assery from Lada. She was built into this amazing, fierce little creature in the first book, but her leadership qualities as well as her dedication to Wallachia really shine in this one.<br/><br/><b>PLOT ➳➳</b><br/>After lea</span>
  <span id="freeText1069842736033527943" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896510860" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> ★★★★★<br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1969388996" rel="nofollow noopener">Now I Rise</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143076758" rel="nofollow noopener">Bright We Burn</a> ★★★☆☆</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <i>They had nothing better, nowhere else to go. They were loyal to her, and to the hope that perhaps she would find them a place in the world.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>FIVE. FREAKING. STARS.</b> <i>Now I Rise</i> is non-stop action, death, war, betrayal, and general bad-assery from Lada. She was built into this amazing, fierce little creature in the first book, but her leadership qualities as well as her dedication to Wallachia really shine in this one.<br /><br /><b>PLOT ➳➳</b><br />After leaving Mehmed's side to carve out her own path to the throne of Wallachia, Lada Dracul finds herself without allies, assistance, or power to speak of, besides the loyalty of her men. When she finds that Mehmed has not been entirely honest or beneficial to her cause, Lada's rage encourages her to finally embrace the cruelty of her nature and to seek out the throne via any means necessary.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Radu helps Mehmed plot to overtake Constantinople, but the waters become muddied when Radu is sent into the city as a spy and begins to second-guess his own motives as well as the sultan's. Will Radu's love for his childhood friend be enough, or must he, too, find his own way?<br /><br /><b>LADA ➳➳</b><br /><b>"Why must I always be a man's servant? If anything, I should be partners with the devil, not his servant."</b><br /><br />She's incredible. I honestly just couldn't help but grin at so many of her remarks and witticisms throughout the book, and I love every second of how devoted her men are to her. She so blatantly refuses to be held down by any man. When it is brought to her attention that her ideals for her people are so vastly different from the plans of the men currently in power, rather than adjust her scheming, she just starts taking what she feels is rightfully hers. She is brutal, wicked, at times shameful, but overall... there's just such solid character development. I could wax on for hours about how much I love Lada Dracul.<br /><br /><b>RADU ➳➳</b><br />Much like in the first book, the chapters alternate viewpoints between Lada and her brother, Radu. Let me preface what I'm about to say with one fact: I <i>loved</i> Radu in the bulk of the first book. I thought he was sweet, kind, charismatic, and just an altogether really likable protagonist. After reading this book, however... I can't go into much detail without spoiling massive plot lines, so all I will tell you is that Radu's opinions of Mehmed are so high that it leads him into some very unsavory situations.<br /><br />That said, Radu is not a <i>bad</i> character. He's infuriating at times, but he's also complex, well-written, dedicated, and loyal to a fault. Despite how much some of his decisions made me want to scream (one of his choices did make me actually slam the book shut), I still loved seeing things through his eyes, and watching him interact with the world around him. I'd love to shout a gigantic "THANK YOU!" to Kiersten for having perfected the task of writing a character that I can absolutely rage at, yet thoroughly love at the same time.<br /><br /><b>WORLD BUILDING ➳➳</b><br />Beyond Lada and Radu themselves, there is such a wonderful and rich cast of characters in this book; we don't meet many new people, but we get to spend a lot more time with some of the lesser characters from <i>And I Darken</i>, and there are some beautiful developments that take place. The politics are still heavy, but not as overwhelming as I found them to be at times in the first book. Kiersten did such a great job of building the world in the first book, that she had to spend <i>very</i> little time expanding upon it in this book, which is a big portion of why I loved this so much more than the first one.<br /><br /><b>FINAL VERDICT ➳➳</b><br />All in all, this book was absolutely incredible and has solidified <i>The Conqueror's Saga</i> as my favorite historical fiction of all time, as well as one of my top series picks. I can't wait for the final release in this series, and to see where Lada and Radu's adventures will bring them in the end. I would recommend this series to anyone who enjoys historical fiction, heavy politics, plenty of violence, and enough back-stabbing and conniving to last you for ages.<br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to Kiersten White and the lovely folks at Delacorte Press for sending me an ARC of this book! My opinions in this review are entirely my own.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1069842736033527943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2002076377" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2002076377" />
    <a title=";3" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34613428-3"><img alt=";3" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548485909p2/34613428.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2002076377?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2017</a>
