<div id="review_2211837262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2211837262" />
    <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson"><img alt="Whitney Atkinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550868411p2/14457130.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2211837262?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney Atkinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney Atkinson" href="/user/show/14457130-whitney-atkinson">Whitney Atkinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favs-of-2017">favs-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14457130-whitney-atkinson?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2211837262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11904898695169847996">4.5 stars<br/><br/>This series continues to amaze me just because of its depth and scope. For a while I thought this book was just boring politics, but then I realized that it continues to play with the themes of identity and religion/culture. But in this book, it also questions loyalty and morality and it’s just??? so good????? I don’t want this to sound like I’m shitting on other YA books but this is seriously so thought-provoking and mature (not in its content, really, just that it tackles so many them</span>
  <span id="freeText11904898695169847996" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />This series continues to amaze me just because of its depth and scope. For a while I thought this book was just boring politics, but then I realized that it continues to play with the themes of identity and religion/culture. But in this book, it also questions loyalty and morality and it’s just??? so good????? I don’t want this to sound like I’m shitting on other YA books but this is seriously so thought-provoking and mature (not in its content, really, just that it tackles so many themes and creates such depth of characters) that I can’t believe more people don’t talk about it. The way that it tackles feelings of belonging and religion and loyalty are so impactful and strangely relatable even though this takes place 600 years ago. it’s just absolutely fascinating.<br /><br />The biggest thing I admire about these books is how much they read like character studies. Lada and Radu are genuinely two of the most interesting characters in YA right now, in my opinion. AND PPL ARE SLEEPING ON IT!!! I cannot emphasize how much I adore Lada as a character. She is ruthless and doesn’t care about others’ opinions of her and does what she think is best for her and is so self-motivated and self-confident, AND YET there’s still this vulnerable and human side to her that craves validation and it makes her so real. And this passion and feeling isn’t even driven by romantic feelings—it’s about duty and feminism and family and morality and IT’S JUST SO GOOD SHE’S SUCH AN INTRICATE AND WELL-CRAFTED CHARACTER. Nothing about her is glossed over. She has periods, she has casual sex, she kills people who betray her, she cries, she is generous. I’m so impressed at the quality of her character.<br />And likewise for Radu. I just……. he’s incredible. The complete opposite of Lada. He wears his heart on his sleeve and he’s outwardly passionate and intelligent and emotional, but there’s a darker, melancholy side to him and his coming to terms with religion and feeling in-between cultures and his sexuality and his feelings of estrangement from his family. I was genuinely crying by the end of this book when he was having to justify being in war and feeling torn between the two cultures and not being able to escape with blood on his hands. i just want to hug him and wrap him in blankets. <br />And the two of these characters together in one book? As brother and sister? Working together? I’m hooked on every page. Even though they are separated throughout this entire book, I couldn’t choose whose POV was my favorite and I never wished they were together just so that the plot would be more interesting. It carried its own weight magnificently. The machinations of their brains drive the story despite their being apart and in this book, the angst and the tension continues to build. It’s addicting.<br /><br />One of my only complaints is that it’s so hard to keep characters, nations, and events straight in this book. I don’t know much about Ottoman or European history, and not much is given explanation-wise. I mean, obviously there’s tension between Muslims and Christians, but I feel like White should have used the opportunity to make this more comprehensible by adding information about the countries and basic history that we should know, because I seriously always forget who’s fighting who and why and who is avenging who and why they died and why does Mehmed want to capture Constantinople and was Constantinople a real place and are these descriptions historically accurate? It pulled me out of the story to be constantly questioning what was happening. Is Constantinople in Turkey? If so, why are they fighting with the Ottomans? Why are there so many Italians? Is it in Italy? Do I have to google 15th century European geography just to understand this book? (Yes.) ((Also, googling Constantinople spoils the war in this book soooo))<br /><br />[side note: the entire problem stated above could probably be solved with a bigger/better map]<br /><br />One more thing that I think would have made this book stronger would have been the addition of Mehmed’s POV. I know the book is centralized on the Wallachian siblings for a reason and it would have been 100+ pages longer with the added perspective, but everyone is split up and I think it works, but knowing what’s going on with the Ottomans would round out the story and help the readers reason with how they should feel about Mehmed, because he’s in a very grey area in this book. He’s the link between the two siblings, a romantic love interest, and the leader of a powerful empire, but for the majority of this book, i wasn’t sure if i was supposed to be rooting for him or not. <br /><br />This is such a slow-burning but strong series. I highly, highly recommend it. It contains some of the most dynamic, fleshed-out characters I’ve ever read in YA, on the level of Cassie Clare &amp; Maggie Stiefvater. Don’t let the slowness of the plot and thickness of the books deceive you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11904898695169847996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2565611842" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2565611842" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2565611842?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2565611842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5195306333987192673"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540670021i/26509806._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Hatred makes monsters of us all.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, I’ll be honest with you, I have been dreading writing this review. I don’t know what’s wrong with me or my reading tastes, but this series just isn’t the series for me. So many of my friends love this series more than anything and you should check out their reviews: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004756407?book_show_action=true&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chaima</a> (Muslim ownvoices), <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792130445?book_show_action=true&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Elise</a>, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618844157?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>Emily</a>! But, sadly, I’m calling it quits and I’m not reading the third book. And if you want my honest opinion? Read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358217257' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Traitor Baru Cormora</a></span>
  <span id="freeText5195306333987192673" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1540670021i/26509806._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Hatred makes monsters of us all.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, I’ll be honest with you, I have been dreading writing this review. I don’t know what’s wrong with me or my reading tastes, but this series just isn’t the series for me. So many of my friends love this series more than anything and you should check out their reviews: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004756407?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Chaima</a> (Muslim ownvoices), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1792130445?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Elise</a>, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1618844157?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily</a>! But, sadly, I’m calling it quits and I’m not reading the third book. And if you want my honest opinion? Read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358217257" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a>, because it’s a better version of (Radu’s storyline especially) this story. <br><br>I didn’t hate this book by any means, it’s just really a 2.5 star, middle of the road book for me. And I’m going to try to keep this review short, because I completely recognize that this series just doesn’t work for me! But this is a historical reimagining, starring two children during the fall of Constantinople, but one of those children is a genderbent Vlad the Impaler.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The world will destroy her in the end. Too much spark leads to explosions. But your sister will destroy as much as she can before she goes out. She will go down in flames and blood.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Lada is my favorite. She’s cutthroat, ruthless, and such a wonderful character to read about. She, to me, is the shining star of this book. Radu, is alright. I enjoyed his storyline in this book, but again, it was so reminiscent of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358217257" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a>, but just done not as well. <br><br>I’ll be honest with you, and this might be a tiny bit spoilery so don’t read any further if you want to go into this tale completely unaware of anything, but I hate love triangles where both siblings like the same person. Maybe it is because I’m so close to my brother, and would never do that to him, but it just makes for a truly painful reading experience. And the character in the middle of it? I hate them with a fiery passion already. <br><br>But what I loved is Kiersten White’s writing. Every book I pick up by the author, blows me away with one-liner after one-liner. Such a beautiful and lyrical writing style, and I gobble it up every book. And it makes me even more excited to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2288336563" rel="nofollow noopener">Slayer</a>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Perhaps she had never stopped being that girl lost in a place where she could never have power.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, I think most people would enjoy this series. Hell, I think most people do enjoy this series. And there really are so many good themes and a lot of representation. So, for sure take my review with a grain of salt. And, again, make sure you check out the reviews of the people I linked in the top paragraph. This series just isn’t for me, and that’s okay. Mehmed is legit the worst character in the history of YA. But Nazira and Fatima are worthy of five stars, though.<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>

<div id="review_1648566008" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648566008" />
    <a title="destini mia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia"><img alt="destini mia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499903277p2/13742215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648566008?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destini mia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destini mia" href="/user/show/13742215-destini-mia">destini mia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13742215-destini-mia?shelf=fierce-leads">fierce-leads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648566008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15389647513392633299"><i>"i don't like lada"<br/><br/>"she's too violent"<br/><br/>"what happened to her compassion"<br/><br/>"she's chang–"</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498788459ra/23162094.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>this book was bomb and lada <b>s l a y e d</b> my entire existence. <br/><i>
  <blockquote>She was a dragon. She was a prince. She was the only hope Wallachia had of ever prospering.<br/>And she would do whatever it took to get there.</blockquote>
</i><br/>she is truly a fearsome thing to behold. so often in novels we get characters that will say they would do anything to accomplish their goals but stop just shy or the author events some miraculous loophole that gi</span>
  <span id="freeText15389647513392633299" style="display:none"><i>"i don't like lada"<br><br>"she's too violent"<br><br>"what happened to her compassion"<br><br>"she's chang–"</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498788459ra/23162094.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>this book was bomb and lada <b>s l a y e d</b> my entire existence. <br><i>
  <blockquote>She was a dragon. She was a prince. She was the only hope Wallachia had of ever prospering.<br>And she would do whatever it took to get there.</blockquote>
</i><br>she is truly a fearsome thing to behold. so often in novels we get characters that will say they would do anything to accomplish their goals but stop just shy or the author events some miraculous loophole that gives the character exactly what they want while keeping their morality and the reader's delicate sensibilities intact. if that's what you like then i would steer clear of this series. <br><br>this is what makes lada such a powerhouse and absolute pleasure to read about. she's makes the hard decisions, she follows through with her threats, and shits on your delicate sensibilities, if you even have them after you've finished book 1.<br><i>
  <blockquote>Radu had been wrong. There were no good men in this city.<br>And there were no good men outside of it, either.</blockquote>
</i><br>now, my precious cinnamon roll radu was a pleasant surprise. kierstan white lit a fire under the ass that is radu's character development. he still has a ways to go but i was shocked at how much i enjoyed his chapters. i suppose it's kind of sad that his innocence and naïveté has been lost but i was also strangely proud that he was seeing the world for what it was. <br><br>the writing was really enjoyable and was able to contribute greatly to the world-building while also allowing the reader to feel connected to the characters. like book 1, it's written in 3rd person, which is great for rich description but usually lacks in character/reader connection. kierstan white balances this perfectly, which is kinda a bitch when i'm here <b>s t r u g g l i n g</b> to keep! it! together! <br><br>also, it's kind of daunting going into a sequel like this without rereading book 1 but i read <i>And I Darken</i> as soon as it came out last year (???) and didn't brush up before starting <i>Now I Rise</i> and while i have no doubt it would help if you did some catching up, i didn't find it absolutely necessary. and this is coming from someone who has the memory retention of a birb. <br><br>i'm glad with the progression of the storyline, overall. did it kinda feel like a bridge book? eh, maybe a little. we don't end on a cliffhanger, per se, but <i>Now I Rise</i> ends clearly setting up for book 3. <br><br>and that ending... lada's response *kisses fingers like a chef* i lived for it<br><br> (and no autocorrect, it's not LADY it's <s>lada</s> DRAGON) <br><i>
  <blockquote>The woman nodded, then dipped her head in a bow. "We owe you everything."<br>Lada smiled. "Do not forget it. I promise I will not.</blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15389647513392633299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1806119303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1806119303" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1806119303?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of And I Darken</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=triggers">triggers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=best-young-adult">best-young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=dark-haired-heroine">dark-haired-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=cover-ecstasy">cover-ecstasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=excellent-writing">excellent-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=gives-me-goosebumps">gives-me-goosebumps</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=mind-blowing-cliffhanger">mind-blowing-cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=intiguing-concept">intiguing-concept</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1806119303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2999315059089056779"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><i>And true to its word this book is more brutal, more ruthless, and stakes were never this high before.</i> Reading <i>And I Darken</i> was not an easy experience for me, but <i>Now I Rise</i> doubles it in intensity and heartbreak. When you have to chose between people you love and right and wrong, things get very messy. There’s no white or black, everything’s gray and painful. <br/><br/>Once again <i>Kiersten White</i> i</span>
  <span id="freeText2999315059089056779" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><i>And true to its word this book is more brutal, more ruthless, and stakes were never this high before.</i> Reading <i>And I Darken</i> was not an easy experience for me, but <i>Now I Rise</i> doubles it in intensity and heartbreak. When you have to chose between people you love and right and wrong, things get very messy. There’s no white or black, everything’s gray and painful. <br /><br />Once again <i>Kiersten White</i> immerses us into the history <i>Ottoman Empire</i> and she does it with style. She lets us observe the events without intervening, without imposing her opinion on readers, but simply letting us choose what side we’d prefer. I am not very good with history, but this book (and the previous one) made we want to know more about this period of time, to learn about real historical figures who are main characters in this series. Granted, the author is more frivolous with historical events in book 2 than she was in book 1, but still you won’t miss out on major events and dates, which author describes with diligence. But no, all of it is secondary and unimportant compared to characters. <b>They are the soul, they are what make history come off the pages and breathe.</b> We will never know what real Lada (Vlad), Radu or Mehmed thought, how close or distant they were to each other, but reading Kiersten White’s version of these people made we believe this is exactly how they were in real life, how they thought and lived. It’s not about truth or lies, it’s about a soul.<br /><br />In And I Darken Lada, doubtless, was the star of the book. A fierce girl who wanted to go home and make everything better. Lada was brutal but also naïve and that made her so human, so vulnerable. In this book… I don’t know what happened to Lada, but she became almost unbearable. Her obsession with <i>Wallachia</i> bordered on madness and foolishness. She was like a broken record player stuck at the same note in a song. Maybe it’s how things should be and Lada’s slowly turning into a ruthless monster is what it is suppose to be, but my heart hurt no mater what, because I got attached to these characters, and <b>it’s still hard to accept the new Lada who betrays friends, kills children and spares no one if they don’t serve her purpose</b>. She doesn’t fight her inner demons any longer, she embraces them and her conscience is barely bothered with her cruelty. Lada still doubts and regrets things, but there’s getting less and less things to regret for her. <br /><br /><b>Radu, on the other hand, is a star of this book.</b> His struggles were so real, so humane, so heartbreaking I wanted to cry. In this part he finds himself in the situation when friends become strangers and enemies become friends. He no longer knows what is right or wrong, but <b>he still fights for truth, for clarity</b>. He doesn’t want to embrace his dark side, he struggles with his inner demons. And I loved Radu for it, because he reminded me of myself and, doubtless, many other people who ever found themselves in a situation when they wanted to do the right thing but didn’t know how. <b>Radu has a phenomenal character development in this book</b>. Plus, I really loved that finally Radu met someone deserving him, unlike Mehmed whom Radu always loved but who would never love him back. <b>Radu deserves all the happiness in the world.</b><br /><br />Mehmed… is still Mehmed, meaning that I am still torn about his character. He seems different when he’s with Radu or Lada, but his actions and deeds show us his sly, ruthless side. He seems like two different persons, but as we see Mehmed only from the siblings’ points of view it’s understandable they are idealizing him, because they love him, and he loves them too, it shows in his actions when he’s with them. But again, betrayal is one of the main threads that goes through this book, and anyone can betray a person they love, because of their ambition. By the way, I need to underline that <b>Mehmed and Lada are very much alike: they are both moved by their ambitions, Radu, on the other hand, is moved by loyalty and love and morale, which makes him the purest of them all. </b><br /><br />Of course, I cannot not mention <b>my favorite topic: siblings relationship</b>. Lada and Radu do not meet in this book. Not once. But they think about each other a lot. <b>They are a balanced pair: Radu is light, Lada is dark, and even miles away from each other they think what Lada or Radu would do in that or this situation.</b> It helps them to do something less ruthless (in the case of Lada), or embrace oneself for something ruthless (in the case of Radu). It breaks my heart thinking that their story would not end well, and there’s a possibility when one of them would have to kill the other. See, this is why this series is so hard to read, because even when you love someone you still might betray them. <i>Brutal from the capital B.</i> <br /><br />Kiersten's writing is superb as ever, plus <b>I absolutely adored politics and intrigues and the way she inserted religion in this book.</b> It played a great role in book 1 as well, but in this one the game is upped and religion has taken the front seat. We all know that people were ready to do monstrous things because God "said" them to do it. But everything was always about ambition and power, and religion was and <i>is</i> a great instrument to level and manipulate opponents. Both <i>Islam and Christianity</i> call the other infidels, but in reality there’s no such thing - only fighting for superiority. And Radu is in the center of that fight, and he sees what righteousness can do to good people, turning them into monsters. There's no good people on this side of the wall, as there's no good people on the other side, as well.<br /><br />&gt;&gt; You haven't yet started <i>The Conqueror's Saga</i>? You are missing a lot on something deliciously vicious. <b>This trilogy is not your typical YA; it's mature, it's dark, it's perfect.</b> You want the history of 15th century <i>Eastern Europe</i> and <i>Ottoman Empire</i>? You want to witness the fall of <i>Constantinople</i>? You want siblings relationship? You want <i>Dracula's</i> ascension? <b>Be the witness of wheels of history turning before your eyes.</b> I promise, you won't regret it.<br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Hold hands with the devil until you are both over the bridge.<br />Or kill the devil and burn the bridge so no one can get to you.” </blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><i>*All quotes in this review are taken form ARC and can be subjected to change*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2999315059089056779" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1533547186" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1533547186" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1533547186?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1533547186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5568815001105201359">The best <s>YA</s> historical fiction series in quite some time. This is one of those series that is so good, you don't want to risk giving any spoilers because it's just that good. The concept alone should be enough to sell the series: An alternate history with Vlad the Impaler as a girl. And if you haven't heard of Vlad the Impaler - he had a reputation for cruelty throughout Europe and took pleasure in torturing and killing his enemies with his most preferred method being impalement. He was also the</span>
  <span id="freeText5568815001105201359" style="display:none">The best <s>YA</s> historical fiction series in quite some time. This is one of those series that is so good, you don't want to risk giving any spoilers because it's just that good. The concept alone should be enough to sell the series: An alternate history with Vlad the Impaler as a girl. And if you haven't heard of Vlad the Impaler - he had a reputation for cruelty throughout Europe and took pleasure in torturing and killing his enemies with his most preferred method being impalement. He was also the inspiration for Dracula. Sold yet?<br /><br />The first book follows Lada starting from her birth. Radu is born a year later. And we follow them as they are sent to be raised in the Ottoman courts. They meet Mehmed and all become huge parts of each other's lives. This one is all about Lada trying to retake Wallachia and the fall of Constantinople. It is a clear retelling of actual events and is so fascinating.<br /><br />This book is every bit as brutal and dark as the first book. The setting is outstanding, vivid, and so easy to visualize. It is beautifully written. I began to really appreciate Nazira's connection with Radu. It's a very sweet dynamic and shows how much they truly care about each other. It's hard to not feel sympathy and anger both over the unrequited romance situation. Lada has become even more badass - is that even possible? Apparently because she's cold-blooded and vicious. To be honest, I was loving every second of it.<br /><br />The romance gets a bit on the annoying side at times, but it's far less present in this book than the first. I think it's there to spark emotions in the characters to really make them go there when it comes to being angry or hurt and doing drastic actions.<br /><br />There is more character development here, especially for Radu. Politics and religion play a large part in the events. I enjoyed the different opinions on the taking of Constantinople regarding religion. It is discussed in a non-offensive way and is rather enlightening.<br /><br />I do miss the characters being together. There was something so special in the first book regarding Lada and Radu's sibling relationship. Don't get me wrong..it is still there. But more in the way that Lada recognizes the skills Radu has that she could really use. She realizes she is stronger with her brother by her side. But that won't do her any good with Radu being sent to Constantinople as Mehmed's inside guy.<br /><br />I really enjoyed where the story went. It remained on the unpredictable side keeping me guessing. The ending picked up the pace a great deal leaving me reeling for book three. It's clear we'll be in for one hell of a ride!<br /><br />If you haven't started the series yet, do yourself a favor and go get <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga___1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga, #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener"> And I Darken</a> now. And if you just haven't read the sequel, what are you waiting on??</span>
  <a data-text-id="5568815001105201359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1698582791" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698582791" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1698582791?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well">he-s-so-bad-but-he-does-it-so-well</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=love-wins">love-wins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bubbling-under-5-stars">bubbling-under-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy">my-inner-feminist-cries-with-joy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1698582791" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5122305811691891517"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I think if you had been a boy, perhaps you would have been satisfied with what the world offered you. This is how we are alike. We saw everything that was not ours, and we hungered. Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight for everything. Even when you already have it, you will have to keep fighting to maintain it. You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499689839ra/23258008.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>You know what I love about this series? <b>You have no idea how it's going to end.</b> This is, o</span>
  <span id="freeText5122305811691891517" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I think if you had been a boy, perhaps you would have been satisfied with what the world offered you. This is how we are alike. We saw everything that was not ours, and we hungered. Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight for everything. Even when you already have it, you will have to keep fighting to maintain it. You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499689839ra/23258008.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You know what I love about this series? <b>You have no idea how it's going to end.</b> This is, of course, assuming you're not familiar with the history and figures that inspired it. (Even if you are, you have no idea which bits and pieces White is planning to incorporate.) <br><br>With most novels, you know the hero is going to save the world/get the girl or boy/smash the corrupt system; it's more the how that pulls you in. But with the Conqueror's Saga, you have no clue. It resembles Game of Thrones in its willingness to take risks. Who will be left in the end? Where will they be? <i>Who</i> will they be?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"She was not a lady. She was a dragon, and this whole country would know it before the end."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Now I Rise is admittedly <b>slower-paced than its predecessor.</b> It takes place right after the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27190613.And_I_Darken__The_Conqueror_s_Saga__1_" title="And I Darken (The Conqueror's Saga #1) by Kiersten White" rel="nofollow noopener">And I Darken</a> with the Dracul siblings separated in both mind and location: Lada in Wallachia, fighting for her throne, and Radu at Mehmed's side in the Ottoman Empire and later Constantinople as a spy. <br><br>There's less political intrigue, and <b>more character study.</b> Although a lot happens in retrospect, it takes place slowly over a number of pages, devoting more time to figuring out who Lada and Radu think they are—self-inspection. And I Rise is evenly split between their POVs and their storyline, while vastly different in goal, parallel each other. They often wonder what the other sibling would do in their situation and act on those perceptions. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Be careful, little dragon. You and I were meant for battlefields, not royal courts. Do not start fights you have no weapons for."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499689839ra/23258010.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Both siblings also gradually realize there is more to the enemy. Lada and Hunyadi, who killed her father and older brother, who treats her kindly and sees her as more than a broodmare to pop out sons. Radu and Constantinople, with its ordinary people and emperor and religion. <b>Neither Christianity or Islam are portrayed as evil.</b> I feel that's important to point out. If there's ever a time in modern history where we need to attach a human face to a legion entity, it's now. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think Mehmed is being set up to be the villain, tbh. What he's doing to Radu is eerily similar to what Lada is doing with Bodgan, which it makes me fear for her character—and life.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>As with And I Darken, women play a big part in the narrative. It's not just the Lada; it's Nazira, Lada's nurse, rape survivors... It's a story about celebrating different women as it is penis envy and subverting patriarchy. I don't necessarily agree with Lada's brand of feminism, which still inclines towards acknowledging male identity as power, but I accept it as part of her character. And it is in no way shown to be the sole "right" version. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499689839ra/23258009.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Next book, please? And if Radu doesn't get a happy ending, I will fling myself off the topmost tower of Hogwarts.<br><br><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575244700" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of And I Darken</a><br> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698582800" rel="nofollow noopener">My review of Bright We Burn</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1652555664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1652555664" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1652555664?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32717627-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=historical-highness">historical-highness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1652555664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11604582991007523561">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to the author, Kiersten White, and the publisher, Delacorte Press, for this opportunity.<br/><br/>This is the second instalment in the much-loved And I Darken series. The book is set primarily in the dual perspectives of Lada and Radu, daughter and son of the renowned Vlad Dragwyla, prince of Wallachia, during the nineteenth century. They spent their childhood used as political bargaining chips and lived as wards to the sultan of b</span>
  <span id="freeText11604582991007523561" style="display:none">I received a copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Thank you to the author, Kiersten White, and the publisher, Delacorte Press, for this opportunity.<br /><br />This is the second instalment in the much-loved And I Darken series. The book is set primarily in the dual perspectives of Lada and Radu, daughter and son of the renowned Vlad Dragwyla, prince of Wallachia, during the nineteenth century. They spent their childhood used as political bargaining chips and lived as wards to the sultan of bordering lands. Now Lada wants what is rightfully hers. Wallachia.<br /><br />I adored this book due to Lada's character. She was feisty and fiercesome, stubborn and spirited, troubled and troublesome. She gave a new insight to the historical female, which has so often painted all of its females as wilting roses and distressed damsels. She is the antithesis of this expected role. Much to the horror of many of the males that surround her.<br /><br />I adored how White allowed Lada to become every bit as bloodthirsty and brutal as her father. I also appreciated how she allowed her brother, Radu, to become every bit as delicate as his sister was expected to be. Both were determination to betray what was expected from their genders and to overcome every obstacle in their opposing rise in strength and notoriety. These stereotypical gender roles were turned on their hand and what resulted were two endearing and authentic individuals, set in a well-written and well-structured satire, exploring dense themes and overcoming many gender and genre defining stereotypes. The additional exploration of Radu's sexuality and the implications it would have in his time and in his position also accounted to make this thoroughly intriguing, enlightening, and thought-provoking reading<br /><br />My only point of discord with this book was the confusion over places and people, which came from the density of plot and the time between my reading of the two books. This was quickly forgotten however, as I was re-absorbed into this world and all the blood-soaked action and political intrigue entailed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11604582991007523561" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1720864072" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720864072" />
    <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway"><img alt="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456070558p2/32524334.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720864072?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina (Every Word A Doorway)" href="/user/show/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway">Nina (Every Word A Doorway)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32524334-nina-every-word-a-doorway?shelf=2017-faves">2017-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720864072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10318737096312334432"><blockquote>
  <em>"Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight for everything. Even when you already have it, you will have to keep fighting to maintain it. You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything. Any weakness will undo everything you have accomplished. They will see any crack as evidence that they were right that a woman cannot do what you do."</em>
</blockquote><br/><strong>If you're looking for a Young Adult novel that combines a Vlad the Impaler reimagining with a rich historical setting and a gloriou</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText10318737096312334432" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <em>"Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight for everything. Even when you already have it, you will have to keep fighting to maintain it. You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything. Any weakness will undo everything you have accomplished. They will see any crack as evidence that they were right that a woman cannot do what you do."</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>If you're looking for a Young Adult novel that combines a Vlad the Impaler reimagining with a rich historical setting and a glorious feminist storyline, then <em>The Conqueror's Saga</em> is your address.</strong> This series excites with multi-layered characters and fascinating character dynamics, intriguing political/war schemes and engaging personal endeavours. <em>And I Darken</em> was a slow build-up but I was really intrigued, especially by the sibling leads. The book's ending gave me a hint that I was going to like where Kiersten White was headed with this story, and I was right.<br><br><strong>Though <em>Now I Rise</em> is split into Lada's and Radu's separate storylines, it does not feel like a filler book. Compared to <em>And I Darken</em>, the sequel is grittier and bloodier. The stakes are raised, as each sibling yearns and fights to be something their harsh world will not permit them to be.</strong><br><br>Let's cut straight to the point: This series will not appeal to everyone, mainly because the pacing is slower than the average YA book's. Kiersten White takes her sweet time with plot advancement in favour of character development. But listen, few authors create characters as beautifully flawed as Kiersten White does, and you just have to appreciate these little cinnamons buns. But I digress. For readers who despise books with story threads that barely meet – and subplots involving quests and journeys, for that matter –, <em>Now I Rise</em> is going to be a disappointment.<strong> I, for one, thought that the separate storylines stood well enough on their own, carried by two engaging leads. </strong>Even without Lada and Radu physically interacting, their mental presence in each other's lives creates a fascinating sibling dynamic. Having reached an impasse in <em>And I Darken</em>, the (half) siblings go separate ways in <em>Now I Rise</em>, each going after their hearts' desire – a throne and a sultan.<br><br>One of this trilogy's appeals is definitely its gender swap which made a feminist take on Vlad the Impaler possible. Men are handed down thrones whereas Lada has to fight for hers. <strong>What speaks to me about Lada's storyline is that she prioritises her homeland and her birthright over romance.</strong> This is such a breath of fresh air compared to all the lovestruck heroines we get, especially in Young Adult novels. Kiersten White pitches a sultan raised with old-fashioned (aka sexist) beliefs against feminist Lada, and thus skillfully sets up two opposite mindsets to clash. <strong>
  <em>Now I Rise </em>
</strong><strong>delivers further evidence as to why this is a Vlad the <em>Impaler</em> reimagining. </strong>Though Lada has always been a character with more edges than a knife, her failures only sharpen her determination and ingenuity, her bitterness and brutality in the sequel. It hardly needs mentioning that witty banter is a standard element of Lada's group of loyal followers. <strong>The only issue I experienced with <em>Now I Rise</em> was that some stops of Lada's quest seemed redundant to the overall plot.</strong> In a book with a slow pacing, every step a character takes needs to be crucial to the outcome, or it will start to feel dragging.<br><br>While Lada is off slaughtering her way through Eastern Europe, Radu is sent to Constantinople as a spy for Mehmed. <strong>Historically, <em>Now I Rise</em> is set before and during the fall of Constantinople under the Ottoman Empire. </strong>Radu's storyline made me realise two things: 1) With her wits and unwavering loyalty, Nazira is the second best female character on this cast, and 2) I need him to be happy with a certain handsome lad from Cyprus and drop his infatuation with Mehmed. The precious, brittle character that is Radu has a lot to stomach in this sequel. He endures the fear of being found out (on a double account!), the horrors of siege and war, and the weight of having his loyalties torn. <strong>Where character development is concerned, Radu makes more progress than Lada, in my opinion.</strong> I'm eagerly waiting to find out what crucial role Radu is going to play in this trilogy's final instalment, and I can only pray that Kiersten White shares my ultimate goal: Radu's happiness.<br><br>This author's skills for crafting fleshed out characters, rich settings, and exquisite prose certainly speak for themselves. But what she truly seems to have a knack for is cliffhangers. <strong>Similar to the first book, <em>Now I Rise</em> ends with a well-aimed punch that'll have you flailing. </strong>Though things have already grown tense between Lada, Radu, and Mehmed, shit is sure to hit the fan in the final instalment.<br><br><strong><em>Now I Rise</em> promises conquests, schemes, tough decisions, heartbreak, and some impaling, and it delivers on all of those. This book is definitely among my favourite reads of 2017. If you're worried the lack of interaction between Lada and Radu or the 'quest plot' are going to impact your reading experience negatively, I can assure you that each subplot adds enough spice to the soup, and Lada's bickering, plotting, and impaling creates sufficient action for any journey.  </strong><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>She knew now that nothing she could do would ever be enough. Unless she could grow a penis, which did not seem likely. Nor particularly desirable.</em>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506541932ra/24026807.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="10318737096312334432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1970387054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1970387054" />
    <a title="alana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12402009-alana"><img alt="alana ♡" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599221603p2/12402009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1970387054?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="alana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="alana ♡" href="/user/show/12402009-alana">alana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553522358" href="/book/show/22817331-now-i-rise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=from-publisher">from-publisher</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=reviewed-arcs">reviewed-arcs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12402009-alana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1970387054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10789180139168377436"><p>
  <em>"No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting"</em>
</p><br/><p>
  <strong>Happy release day to this light fluffy read that will warm your heart!</strong>
</p><br/><strong>Rating: 4.5/5</strong><br/><br/>I received an ARC of this and I can finally post my review now that it's release day :)<br/><br/>In case you couldn't tell guys that is COMPLETE sarcasm. There is nothing light, fluffy, or heartwarming about this book yet it is still AMAZING. <em>Now I Rise </em>is the sequel to <em>And I Darken</em> and let me tell you this book 1. did </span>
  <span id="freeText10789180139168377436" style="display:none"><p>
  <em>"No one will be more brutal than me. No one will be more ruthless. And I will never stop fighting"</em>
</p><br /><p>
  <strong>Happy release day to this light fluffy read that will warm your heart!</strong>
</p><br /><strong>Rating: 4.5/5</strong><br /><br />I received an ARC of this and I can finally post my review now that it's release day :)<br /><br />In case you couldn't tell guys that is COMPLETE sarcasm. There is nothing light, fluffy, or heartwarming about this book yet it is still AMAZING. <em>Now I Rise </em>is the sequel to <em>And I Darken</em> and let me tell you this book 1. did not disappoint 2. did not drag at times like A<em>nd I Darken </em>did and 3. crushed my soul into a million pieces for two people and two people only, and those are my precious babies Lada and Radu. From the first page of this book to the very last it is filled with nothing but death, heartache, betrayal, ruthlessness, and of course Lada slaying my entire existence. I would love to know how many hours Kiersten White has poured into research for this book because it clearly shows with how in depth the story goes.<br /><br />Lada, in <em>Now I Rise</em>, is like no other female character we have ever met before (or probably ever will because let's be realistic it is going to take A LOT for another author to ever top her character). I thought Lada was ruthless in book one but LOL NOPE, not even close. She will slaughter anyone who stands in her way of getting the Wallachian throne. Literally anyone. She faces so much sexism throughout this book but the way the author handles it is top notch and really makes you want to fight right beside Lada for her throne. Some of my very favorite quotes that show Lada rising above the sexism and not letting a man define her power include:<br /><p>
  <em>"She knew now that nothing she could do would ever be enough. Unless she could grow a penis, which did not seem likely. Nor particularly desirable."</em>
</p><br /><p>
  <em>"Anger and humiliation wash through her. All this time Hyundai had been viewing her as merely a womb. How could she make the world see her as she saw herself?"</em>
</p><br /><p>
  <em>It was the same choice she had faced before, the only choice ever given to her; take what little power you can through a man."</em>
</p><br /><p>
  <em>"You are no king, and I am no wife. I am a leader and a ruler and I want your support."</em>
</p><br /><p>
  <em>"Do not lose that hunger. You will always have to fight for everything. Even when you already have it, you will have to keep fighting to maintain it. You will have to be more ruthless, more brutal, more everything."</em>
</p><br />And one of personal favorites that shows how Radu views women is:<br /><p>
  <em>""You are here so that everyone sees you are my special project. I want the whole city gossiping about how foolish I am, hiring a woman to make the largest canon in the word to try and impress the sultan. I intent to subject us both to ridicule." Her scowl deepened. "Why would you do that?" "So that no one pays any attention until we succeed.""</em>
</p><br />*QUEUE BEYONCE MUSIC* Who run the world?! GIRLS!<br /><br />Radu, in this book broke my heart but infuriated me at the same time. I hated how he chose a love interest over family. His undying loyalty to the one person who will never love him back or have any type of public relationship with him used him in ways a person shouldn't be used. I think Radu playing both sides of the field (battle field that is) was integral to the story and to his growth as a character. I hope that in book 3 he gets the happy ending that he deserves with anyone but Mehmed. I'm sure it's pretty apparent from all the updates I posted while reading this that I can't stand Mehmed. Honestly, I'm not even going to write about him because this could easily turn into a 10,000 word review on why I hate Mehmed. So let's just leave it at, I hope book 3 comes around and obliterates everything he's ever loved (besides Lada) and that he dies.<br /><br />There are a handful of other characters that we learn more about throughout the story but not many new ones. Which definitely helped because sometimes names could get a little bit confusing for me. We get to see more characters who didn't have that big of a part in <em>And I Darken</em> in this book and learn about their backstories which was totally cool. I'm dying for some more of Nazira come book 3, just sayin'.<br /><br />This book originally came across as intimidating when I first started, so I would definitely recommend brushing up on book one before jumping into this. Also USE THE GLOSSARY IN THE BACK! I didn't realize it was there until the end and it would have been so helpful had I known it was there, stupid me. There seems to be less politics this time around, don't get me wrong it's still there and still SUPER good, but there is a lot more killing going on then anything else. No complaints here. The dual POV makes the book that much easier to devour because Lada and Radu get in some deep shit in this book, switching back and forth between them makes you fly thought it just to make sure everyone is okay.<br /><br />This book doesn't end on a giant cliffhanger which I loved but it sets us up for book 3 which I am very afraid and excited for. I ONLY HOPE IT ENDS BADLY FOR MEHMED, NOT MY LITTLE BABIES.<br /><br />All in all, this is my favorite historical fiction saga I've ever read. It has politics, love death, war, and some humor in all the right places. You can't help put love Lada for the dragon she has become throughout the two books, and I CANNOT wait to see what happens in the next installment. I have a feeling A LOT more heart break and suffering has to happen before Lada and Radu will have a somewhat happy ending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10789180139168377436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
